لكن بقي هاهنا بحث، وهو أنا لا نسلم أن المسامتة ببعض الزاوية أو الحركة قبل المسامتة الحاصلة بكلها وإنما يلزم ذلك إذا كان بعضهما موجودا بالفعل حتى يمكن أن يوجد به مسامتة لكنهما ينقسمان بالقوة لا بالفعل، ولو صح ما ذكرتموه لامتنع حركة نصف قطر الدائرة على قوس منها لأن الحركة إلى نصف القوس قبل الحركة إلى كلها والحركة إلى نصف الزاوية قبل الحركة إلى كلها، وهكذا بل تمتنع الحركة مطلقا، فالشبهة إنما وقعت من موضع ما بالقوة مكان ما بالفعل ودفعه بعض الأفاضل بأن ما ذكرناه أحكام وهمية إلا أنها صحيحة، إذ الوهم إنما يحكم بها على طاعة [؟] من العقل كسائر الهندسيات، فليس المدعى إلا أنه لا بد للمسامتة الحادثة من أول نقطة في الوهم لكن الخط الغير المتناهي لا يتعين فيه نقطة للأولية بخلاف الخط المتناهي وفيه نظر. إذ ليس يلزم من حدوث المسامتة إلا أن يكون لها زمان هو أول أزمنة وجودها فلا تكون المسامتة الحادثة فيه مسبوقة بمسامتة في زمان سابق عليه وهذا اللازم لا يستلزم أن يوجد هناك نقطة هي أول نقط المسامتة في الوهم بيانه أن نقول: لا مسامتة حال الموازاة بل لا بد لحدوثها من حركة واقعة في زمان فإذا وجدت كانت المسامتة حاصلة في كل آن يفرض في ذلك الزمان وتلك الآنات المفروضة فيه غير متناهية أي لا تقف عند حد، فكذا المسامتات المتوهمة فيها وكل واحدة منها إنما هي نقطة أخرى فلا نقطة أولى يقف الوهم عندها وهل هذا إلا مثل أن يقال: لو حدثت الحركة لكان لها أول زمان توجد فيه وحينئذ فلا بد أن يتعين لها ولمسامتتها جزء أول في الوهم لكنه محال لا يقال: المسامتة آنية فلا بد لها من نقطة غير مسبوقة بأخرى في الوهم لأنا نقول: مسامتة الخط للنقطة آنية وأما المسامتة المذكورة أعني مسامتة الخط للخط فلا يتصور حدوثها إلا بوجود حركة في زمان كما ذكرناه فليس هناك مسامتة إلا وهي مسبوقة في الوهم بأخرى إلى غير النهاية فلا يتعين فيه نقطة غير مسبوقة ويمكن أن يقال: نحن ندعي أنه إذا وقع ذلك المفروض في الخارج فلا بد أن يتعين فيه نقطة هي أول نقط المسامتة إذ لا بد هناك من مسامتة غير مسبوقة فيه بأخرى وإلا لزم وجود مسامتات غير متناهية العدد بالفعل في زمان متناه وهو محال فتلك المسامتة إنما هي بأولى النقط، ولك أن تحمل ذلك الدفع على هذا المعنى بأن تجعل تعين النقطة في الوهم عبارة عن تعينها في الخارج على تقدير وقوع المفروض فيه فيندفع النظر عنه.
But there remains here a discussion, which is that we do not concede that contact occurs by a part of the angle or motion before the contact achieved by the whole; rather, that would follow only if a part of them existed actually so that contact could occur by it, but they are divided potentially, not actually. And if what you mentioned were correct, the motion of a radius of a circle on its arc would be impossible, because motion to half the arc is before motion to the whole, and motion to half the angle is before motion to the whole, and so on; rather, motion would be absolutely impossible. So the confusion arose only from treating a potential part as an actual one. And some virtuous scholars refuted it by saying that what we mentioned are estimative judgments, but they are correct, for the estimation only judges them in obedience [؟] to reason like other geometrical truths. So the claim is only that the occurring contact must have a first point in estimation, but the infinite line has no point determined for priority, unlike the finite line. But there is consideration: it does not follow from the occurrence of contact except that it has a time that is the first of its times of existence, so the contact occurring in that time is not preceded by a contact in a time before it; this necessity does not entail that there exists a point that is the first point of contact in estimation. Its explanation: we say there is no contact during parallelism, but for its occurrence there must be a motion occurring in time. When it occurs, contact is present in every instant assumed in that time, and those assumed instants in it are infinite, i.e., they do not stop at a limit; likewise the imagined contacts in it, and each of them is another point, so there is no first point at which estimation stops. Is this not like if it were said: if motion occurred, it would have a first time in which it exists, and then it must have and its contact must have a first part in estimation, but it is impossible? It cannot be said: contact is instantaneous, so it must have a point unpreceded by another in estimation, because we say: contact of a line with a point is instantaneous, but the mentioned contact, i.e., contact of a line with a line, cannot be conceived to occur except through the existence of motion in time as we mentioned, so there is no contact except that it is preceded in estimation by another ad infinitum, so no point unpreceded is determined in it. And it can be said: we claim that if that assumed occurred externally, then a point that is the first point of contact must be determined in it, because there must be a contact unpreceded therein by another, otherwise there would be an actually infinite number of contacts in a finite time, which is impossible; so that contact is only with the first point. And you may interpret that refutation in this sense by making the determination of the point in estimation an expression of its determination externally on the assumption of the occurrence of the assumed in it, then the consideration is refuted.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is a discussion (بحث) that follows the previous responses. The author raises a further objection: contact by a part of the angle or motion before the whole would require those parts to be actual, but they are only potential. This is clarified by the example of a radius moving on an arc; if the objection held, motion would be impossible entirely. The confusion stems from treating potential as actual. A virtuous scholar (بعض الأفاضل) responds that these are estimative (وهمية) judgments, but valid because estimation follows reason in geometrical matters. The claim is only that occurring contact has a first point in estimation, but the infinite line cannot have a determinate first point. However, the author notes a consideration (نظر): the occurrence of contact only requires a first time, not a first point in estimation. Detailed explanation: during parallelism there is no contact; motion in time yields contact at every instant; these instants are infinite, so no first point. The analogy is given of motion having a first time. The passage distinguishes contact of line with point (instantaneous) vs. line with line (requires motion over time). Finally, a possible reply is offered: if the scenario occurs externally, a first contact point must exist in reality to avoid an actual infinite in finite time; this can be reconciled with the previous refutation by identifying determination in estimation with determination externally. The passage follows a dialectical structure: objection, response, counter-response, and reconciliation.

Key Terms
بالقوة
بالفعل
مسامتة
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That contact requires an actual part of the angle or motion.
Correction: Parts of motion and angle are only potential; thus the requirement cannot be met.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, why does the argument requiring contact by a part of the angle fail?
A) Because such parts are actual
B) Because such parts are only potential, not actual
C) Because motion is impossible
D) Because contact is instantaneous

Key Takeaway
Mistaking potential parts for actual leads to logical contradictions, such as the impossibility of motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever made a decision based on a possibility that you treated as already certain, only to realize later that your reasoning was flawed? How can you better distinguish between what is merely potential and what is actual in your life from now on?
?
This lesson reveals that confusing potential with actual can lead to logical absurdities. In your spiritual journey, are there good deeds or habits you keep 'in potential'—intending to do them but never actualizing? What is one thing you will turn from potential to actual today?
?
The author exposes a fallacy that seemed plausible. Are there beliefs or assumptions you hold that might be based on a similar mistake—treating what is only conceptual as if it is real? What would it cost you to examine those assumptions honestly and correct them?

Refutation: Estimative Reasoning and Infinite Continuity
Al-Isfahani presents the refutation, counter-argument, and final resolution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of the objection through estimative reasoning, the distinction between first time and first point in estimation, and the resolution involving actual infinite contacts.

Core Idea
Contact in estimation has no first point due to infinite divisibility, but externally a first contact must exist.

After diagnosing the fallacy, the author presents a refutation by a virtuous scholar using estimative judgments. However, he counters with a key distinction: contact has a first time but not necessarily a first point in estimation. The lesson concludes by reconciling the need for a first point externally to avoid an actual infinite.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the estimative response
Read the response that says contact must have a first point in estimation (وهم). Understand why infinite lines lack a determinate first point.
The response relies on estimative judgments that follow reason.
2
Examine the counter-consideration
Al-Isfahani objects: contact only requires a first time, not a first point in estimation. He explains that contact occurs at every instant in a motion time, and these instants are infinite.
Notice the distinction between time and estimation.
3
Understand the final reconciliation
The last part argues that externally, a first contact point must exist to avoid an actual infinite in finite time. This can be interpreted as the determination in estimation reflecting external determination.
This resolves the earlier consideration.

Counterargument from the author of Lubab al-Arba'in
A later scholar's objection against the proof of finite dimensions is refuted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the attempted reversal of the argument for finite dimensions fails, and how the impossibility of extending a line outside the universe refutes it.

Core Idea
Contact with non-existent points is inconceivable; the universe has no void or plenum.

The author of Lubab al-Arba'in attempts to turn the proof of finite dimensions against its proponents by showing it would imply infinite points. However, the commentator quickly dismisses this objection, pointing out that it relies on imagining contact with points that do not exist outside the universe. This short passage is a crisp example of rebuttal in kalam reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the initial statement by the author of Lubab al-Arba'in and the swift rejection by the commentator.
The passage is dense with technical terms like مسامتة.
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
Divide the passage into the counterargument (up to the first period) and the refutation. Determine where each begins and ends.
The first half gives the counterargument; the second half begins with 'وهذا الذي ذكره مما لا ورود له'.
3
Analyze the counterargument's logic
The counterargument uses a thought experiment with the axis of the world and a parallel line moving to contact it. Work through the steps: axis assumed, line moves, contact with points outside before axis, leading to infinite points.
The key is that it assumes points outside the universe exist for the line to contact.
4
Study the refutation
The refutation argues that contact with non-existent points is inconceivable because no line can extend outside the universe (no void or plenum). Understand why this is a fatal flaw.
This refutation relies on the earlier established fact that there is nothing outside the universe.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال بعض فضلاء المتأخرين وهو صاحب لباب الأربعين: هذا الدليل مقول عليكم لدلالته على عدم تناهي الأبعاد بأن يقال: إن أطول خط يفرض في البعد المتناهي الموجود هو محور العالم فإذا فرضنا خطا يوازيه ثم يتحرك حتى يسامته على طرفه والمسامتة مع النقطة التي فوقه خارج العالم قبل المسامتة معه لما ذكرتم بعينه فيلزم أن يكون على سمته نقط لا تتناهى وبعد غير متناه ينفرض فيه تلك النقط وهذا الذي ذكره مما لا ورود له كيف والمسامتة مع نقطة لا وجود لها لا تعقل لأنه لا يمكن إخراج خط إلى خارج العالم إذ لا خلاء موجودا هناك ولا ملا فكيف يتصور ملاقاته لنقطة معدومة فيه والوهم
And some virtuous later scholars, namely the author of Lubab al-Arba'in, said: This argument is used against you because it indicates the non-finiteness of dimensions, in that: the longest line assumed in the existing finite dimension is the axis of the universe. So if we assume a line parallel to it, then it moves until it contacts it at its end, and the contact with the point above it outside the universe occurs before the contact with it according to what you mentioned exactly; thus it follows that there are infinite points on its path and an infinite distance in which those points are assumed. And this [claim] has no validity. How so? Contact with a point that has no existence is inconceivable, because it is impossible to extend a line outside the universe since there is no void or plenum there; so how can one conceive of its meeting a non-existent point in it? And the estimation...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage presents a counterargument from a later scholar (صاحب لباب الأربعين) who tries to reverse the earlier proof. He argues that if we take the axis of the universe (longest finite line) and imagine a parallel line moving to contact its end, then contact with points outside the universe (which are non-existent) would occur before contact with the axis, leading to infinite points and distance. The commentator immediately rejects this: contact with a non-existent point is inconceivable because no line can extend outside the universe—there is no void or plenum (لا خلاء ولا ملا). Therefore the counterargument has no basis. The passage is a short refutation of an attempted reversal. Key terms include 'axis of the world' (محور العالم), 'void' (خلاء), 'plenum' (ملا), and 'contact' (مسامتة).

محور العالم
خلاء
ملا
مسامتة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The counterargument successfully proves that dimensions are infinite.
Correction: The refutation shows that the argument relies on the impossible scenario of contact with non-existent points outside the universe, so it is invalid.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator reject the counterargument from the author of Lubab al-Arba'in?
A) Because the axis is not the longest line
B) Because contact with non-existent points is impossible
C) Because the universe is infinite
D) Because the motion is impossible

Key Takeaway
The attempted reversal of the finite dimensions proof fails because it depends on the impossible assumption of contact with non-existent points outside the universe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just read that contact with non-existent points outside the universe is inconceivable because there is no void or plenum there. Do you still find yourself imagining 'nothing' beyond the universe? How does this impossibility affect your understanding of Allah's absolute dominion over all that exists? Will you train your mind to accept that the universe is all there is, and that even 'empty space' is a creation?
?
The author of Lubab al-Arba'in built his counterargument on an impossible scenario. Are there beliefs in your own life that rest on assumptions you have not examined? What would it cost you to investigate them honestly before Allah?
?
This lesson argues that the universe is finite—limited in extent. If the universe has an end, then your time in it is short. How will you live differently today knowing that you cannot postpone repentance or good deeds to an endless future? What one thing will you do now to prepare for when the universe itself ends?

Refuting the Void Argument for a Single World
Second proof against another world involving void and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second philosophical proof against another world based on void and how it is refuted by the possibility of a filler or embedding in a larger sphere.

Core Idea
The void between worlds is avoidable through a filler or a larger containing sphere.

This passage presents the second argument against the possibility of another world: if two worlds existed, there would be a void between them, which the philosophers considered impossible. The answer, however, cleverly avoids this consequence by proposing that a filler could occupy the space, or that both worlds could be embedded within a larger sphere—just as celestial spheres contain many bodies. Let's explore this nuanced rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proof's claim
Read the proof carefully: it argues that another world would create a void because contact between spheres is only at a point, and contact with a non-sphere leaves a gap. Since void is impossible, another world is impossible.
Note that the proof assumes the impossibility of void—this is a shared premise.
2
Examine the answer's strategy
The answer grants the impossibility of void but denies that void necessarily follows. It offers two ways to avoid void: a filler occupying the gap, or embedding both worlds in a larger sphere.
The answer does not reject the premise but shows it does not lead to the conclusion.
3
Reflect on the supporting analogy
The answer uses the example of celestial spheres: the sphere of Mars is said to be vast and could contain elements and compounds like ours. This shows that a larger containing sphere is conceivable, making the existence of another world possible.
This step shows the author's method of analogical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: لو وجد عالم آخر لكان بينهما خلاء سواء كانا ( معاً (كرتين (أولا) وذلك لأن هذا العالم كروي فإن كان الآخر كروياً أيضاً لم يتصور الملاقاة بينهما إلا بنقطة فلا بد أن يقع بينهما خلاء سواء تلاقيا أولا، وإن لم يكن كروياً وقع الخلاء أيضاً لأن ملاقاة الكرة لما ليس بكرة لا تكون إلا مع فرجة . (والجواب ) بعد تسليم امتناع الخلاء أن نقول : ( لا نسلم ذلك لجواز أن يملاهما أي يملأ ما بينهما ( ماليء ولو أردنا ذكر مستند للمنع تبرعاً، قلنا: قد يكونان ) أي العالمان (تدويرين) مركوزين (في ثخن (كرة عظيمة يساوي ثخنها قطريهما أو يزيد عليهما ( وربما تتضمن تلك الكرة (ألوفاً) من الكرات كل واحدة منها ( أعظم من المحدد بما فيها من الأفلاك والعناصر ) ولا استبعاد ) في ذلك ( فإنهم قالوا : تدوير المريخ أعظم من ممثل الشمس بما فيها من الأفلاك الثلاثة والعناصر الأربعة ثلاث مرات ) وإذا جاز ذلك فلم لا يجوز فيما هو أعظم منه ؟ ومن أين لكم أنه ليس في جوف تدوير المريخ عناصر ومركبات مماثلة لما عندنا ؟ ) في الحقيقة ( أو مخالفة له فيها
Second: If another world existed, there would be void between them, whether both are spheres or not. That is because this world is spherical. If the other is also spherical, contact between them is conceivable only at a point, so void must occur between them whether they touch or not. If it is not spherical, void also occurs because contact of a sphere with what is not a sphere only occurs with a gap. The answer: After granting the impossibility of void, we say: We do not concede that [there must be void] because it is possible that a filler fills what is between them, i.e., fills the space between them. And if we wish to mention a basis for the denial gratuitously, we say: It is possible that the two worlds are spheres embedded in the thickness of a great sphere whose thickness equals or exceeds their diameters, and perhaps that sphere contains thousands of spheres each of which is greater than the limiter including its spheres and elements. There is no improbability in that, for they said: The sphere of Mars is three times greater than the representative of the sun including its three spheres and four elements. If that is possible, why is it not possible for what is greater than it? And whence do you know that in the interior of the sphere of Mars there are not elements and compounds similar to what we have? In reality, or differing from it?
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof against another world and its answer. The proof argues that another world would necessitate a void between it and this world, whether both are spheres or not, because contact between spheres is only at a point, and between a sphere and non-sphere there is a gap. Since void is impossible, another world is impossible. The answer first grants the impossibility of void but denies that void necessarily follows. It offers two possibilities: either a filler occupies the space between them, or the two worlds are embedded in a larger sphere that fills the gap. The answer further suggests that this larger sphere could contain many worlds, analogous to the celestial spheres, making the existence of another world possible.

Key Terms

الملاقاة
الكرة
التدوير
المريخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that if the impossibility of void is accepted, then another world cannot exist because void would be unavoidable.
Correction: The answer shows that void can be avoided by a filler or by embedding worlds in a larger sphere, so the impossibility of void does not rule out another world.

Checkpoint
What is the main strategy used in the answer to the second proof?
A) Denying that void exists at all.
B) Granting the impossibility of void but showing that void does not necessarily result, via a filler or embedding in a larger sphere.
C) Accepting void and arguing it is not impossible.
D) Shifting the burden of proof to the philosopher.

Key Takeaway
The second proof fails because the void can be eliminated by a filler or by embedding the worlds in a larger sphere, rendering the impossibility of void irrelevant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter an argument that seems logically airtight (like 'void must exist between worlds'), do you immediately accept it, or do you actively search for hidden assumptions or alternative explanations? How might your tendency to accept such arguments limit your trust in God's ability to work beyond your reasoning?
?
The answer uses the vastness of the sphere of Mars to suggest that far greater structures are possible. In what area of your life have you limited God's power because you cannot conceive of a 'larger container' for His action? Will you ask Him to expand your vision today?
?
The philosophers assumed void was impossible and used that to deny other worlds. Are there 'voids' in your faith—uncertainties, doubts, or unanswered questions—that you assume are permanent? Could it be that God has a 'filler' or a 'larger sphere' that you have not yet considered? What step will you take to seek that answer?

First Branch: Celestial Souls Have Intellectual and Physical Powers
Arguments that celestial souls require physical powers for particular motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why celestial souls require physical powers alongside their intellectual power to account for particular motions.

Core Idea
Universal intellection alone cannot cause particular motions; physical imagination is needed.

Having established that celestial spheres have immaterial souls, the author now explains that these souls must also possess physical powers. The reason is that the intellectual power, being universal, cannot specify which particular motion occurs at a given time. This lesson unpacks that argument and describes the nature of those physical powers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author begins with a claim (‘they have…’) and then gives the reason (‘for universal intellection is not suitable…’).
The passage is the first branch, so it starts with 'الأول'.
2
Identify the two types of powers
The passage distinguishes between intellectual power (قوة عقلية) and physical powers (قوى جسمانية). Understand the role of each.
Intellectual power is like our rational soul; physical powers are like imagination.
3
Understand the argument against universal intellection
Why can't universal intellection alone cause particular motions? Because it relates equally to all particulars and cannot specify one without a particular will and perception.
This is the key logical step in the argument.
4
Learn about the nature of these physical powers
The passage describes them as similar to human imagination, but simple and pervading the whole sphere. They are called 'imprinted souls' (نفوس منطبعة).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : لها مع القوة العقلية التي نسبتها إليها كنسبة النفس الناطقة إلينا قوى جسمانية هي بتخيلاتها مبدأ للحركات الجزئية الصادرة عنها فإن التعقل الكلي لا يصلح لذلك أي لكونه مبدأ لوقوع الحركة الجزئية فإن نسبته إلى جميع الجزئيات سواء فلا يصلح مبدأ لتخصيص البعض بالوقوع دون البعض بل لا بد في وقوعه من إرادة جزئية متفرعة من إدراك جزئي لا يتصور إلا من قوة جسمانية، وهذه القوى في الأفلاك كالخيال فينا إلا أنها سارية في جميع أجزائها بسيطة وتسمى نفوساً منطبعة
First: They have, along with the intellectual power whose relation to them is like the relation of the rational soul to us, physical powers that are, by their imaginations, the principle of the particular motions issuing from them. For universal intellection is not suitable for that, i.e., for being a principle for the occurrence of particular motion, because its relation to all particulars is equal, so it is not suitable as a principle for specifying some for occurrence rather than others. Rather, for its occurrence there must be a particular will branching from a particular perception, which is only conceivable from a physical power. These powers in the spheres are like the imagination in us, except that they are permeating all their parts, simple, and are called imprinted souls.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents the first branch (tafri') resulting from the established view that the spheres have immaterial souls. It asserts that besides the intellectual power (al-quwwa al-'aqliyya) which is analogous to our rational soul, the celestial souls also possess physical powers (quwā jismāniyya). These physical powers, through their particular imaginations (takhayyulāt), serve as the principle for particular motions. The reason is that universal intellection, being equally related to all particulars, cannot specify which particular motion should occur at a given time. A specifying principle requires a particular will (irāda juz'iyya) arising from a particular perception (idrāk juz'ī), which can only come from a physical power. These powers are described as similar to the human imaginative faculty (khayāl) but are simple and pervade all parts of the celestial body. They are called 'imprinted souls' (nufūs munṭabi'a).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Celestial souls, being immaterial, cannot have physical powers.
Correction: This branch clarifies that they indeed have physical powers specifically for causing particular motions, which their intellectual power alone cannot account for.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that universal intellection alone cannot cause particular motions?
A) Because it is not powerful enough.
B) Because it relates equally to all particulars and cannot specify one.
C) Because it is located in a physical organ.
D) Because it is finite.

Key Takeaway
Celestial souls combine intellectual power with physical powers like imagination to produce particular motions, because universal intellection alone cannot specify which motion occurs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your daily actions are countless small 'particular motions'. What particular perception of Allah's commands is currently specifying your will to obey Him—or is your will being driven by imaginations disconnected from the truth?
?
The celestial souls use their physical powers intentionally to move the spheres. What physical power (your limbs, your time, your energy) are you using right now to move towards Allah, and are you conscious of the particular perception behind that movement?
?
If you truly believed that universal intellection cannot specify your actions, you would examine every particular perception that enters your mind. What one particular perception, when you dwell on it, produces a will that distances you from Allah—and what will you actively replace it with today?

First Proof for the Intellect as the First Emanation
Al-Jurjani gives the first proof that the first emanation is the intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first philosophical proof that the first emanation from God must be the intellect, based on God's absolute unity and the independence required of the first created being.

Core Idea
The intellect is the only being that can be both simple and independent, making it the necessary first emanation.

Al-Jurjani begins by citing the philosophers' statement and a Prophetic hadith about the first creation. He then explains how different hadiths can be reconciled. The core of the lesson is the first proof: because God is absolutely one, only one thing can proceed directly from Him, and that thing cannot be composed or dependent. This leads to the conclusion that the first emanation must be the intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the argument is structured: a hadith citation, reconciliation, then the proof.
The Arabic includes key technical terms like 'واحد حقيقي' (truly one) and 'الصادر الأول' (first emanation).
2
Understand the hadith reconciliation
The author explains that the same reality (the first effect) can be called 'intellect', 'Pen', and 'light' depending on different aspects. This reconciles three hadiths.
This shows the compatibility between revelation and philosophical reasoning.
3
Follow the elimination of candidates
The proof eliminates body, part, accident, and soul as candidates for the first emanation, each for a specific reason. Trace each reason.
Body is composed (implies multiplicity), part is incomplete, accident depends on substance, soul depends on body.
4
Grasp the conclusion and summary
Only the intellect remains, as it is simple, independent in existence and effect. Read the summary at the end.
The summary condenses the argument into three conditions: oneness, independence in existence, and independence in effect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الأول : في إثبات العقل في إثباته قال الحكماء : أول ما خلق الله تعالى العقل كما ورد نص الحديث ( قلماً، عقلاً ) ومن قال بعضهم : وجه الجمع بينه وبين الحديثين الآخرين أول ما خلق الله القلم وأول ما خلق الله نوري أن المعلول الأول من حيث إنه مجرد يعقل ذاته ومبدؤه يسمي ومن حيث أنه واسطة في صدور سائر الموجودات ونفوس العلوم يسمى حيث توسطه في إفاضة أنوار النبوة كان نوراً لسيد الأنبياء واحتجوا عليه أي على إثبات العقل بوجهين : الأول : الله تعالى واحد حقيقي لا تكثر فيه أصلاً بوجه من الوجوه فلا يصدر عنه ابتداء إلا الواحد ويمتنع أن يكون ذلك الصادر عنه جسماً لتركبه فلو صدر أولاً لزم تعدد الصادر في المرتبة الأولى ولتقدم الهيولى والصورة عليه ضرورة لأن الجزء متقدم على الكل فلو كان هو الصادر الأول لتقدم على أجزائه ، ولا يجوز أيضاً أن يكون الصادر الأول أحد جزأيه إذ لا يستقبل بالوجود دون الآخر فلا يستقل بالتأثير أيضاً والصادر الأول مستقل بالوجود والتأثير معاً ولا عرضاً إذ لا يستقل بالوجود دون الجوهر الذي هو محله فكيف يوجد قبله ولا نفساً إذ لا تستقل بالتأثير دون الجسم الذي هو آلتها فيمتنع أن يكون سبباً لما بعده ويجب ذلك فيما صدر أولاً فتعين أن يكون الصادر الأول هو العقل. تلخيصه أول صادر عنه تعالى واحد مستقل بالوجود والتأثير، وغير العقل ليس كذلك لانتفاء القيد الأول في الجسم، والثاني في الهيولى والصورة والعرض، والثالث في النفس.
The First Intention: On the Proof of the Intellect. Concerning its proof, the philosophers said: The first thing God created is the intellect, as is mentioned in the text of the hadith ('aql). And some said: The reconciliation between it and the other two hadiths, 'The first thing God created is the Pen' and 'The first thing God created is my light', is that the first effect, insofar as it is simple ('free from matter') and intellects its essence and its Principle, is called 'aql; and insofar as it is a medium in the emanation of the rest of existents and the souls of the sciences, it is called 'Pen'; and due to its mediation in the bestowal of the lights of prophethood, it was the 'light' of the Chief of the Prophets. And they argued upon it (i.e., for the proof of the intellect) by two proofs. The first: God is one, truly one, having no multiplicity at all in any respect; therefore, only one can proceed from Him in the first instance. And it is impossible that that which proceeds from Him is a body, due to its composition; for if it proceeded first, multiplicity of proceeding would follow at the first rank, and the primacy of hyle and form over it [would follow] necessarily, because the part is prior to the whole; so if it were the first proceeding, it would be prior to its parts. Nor is it permissible that the first proceeding be one of its two parts, for it does not receive existence without the other, nor is it independent in effect; the first proceeding is independent in existence and effect together. Nor [can it be] an accident, for it is not independent in existence without the substance which is its substrate; how then could it exist before it? Nor a soul, for it is not independent in effect without the body which is its instrument; therefore it is impossible for it to be a cause for what is after it. This is necessary for that which proceeds first. So it is determined that the first proceeding is the intellect. Summary: The first proceeding from Him, exalted, is one, independent in existence and effect; and other than the intellect is not like that, because the first condition is absent in the body, the second in hyle and form and accident, and the third in the soul.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents the first of two proofs for the existence of the intellect as the first emanation. The author begins by citing the philosophers' saying and a hadith, then explains a reconciliation between different hadiths. The core argument: God is absolutely one, so only one thing can proceed from Him directly. That first thing cannot be a body (because bodies are composed, implying multiplicity), nor a part of a body (not independent), nor an accident (needs a substance), nor a soul (needs a body to act). Therefore, it must be an intellect, which is a simple substance independent of matter. The author then summarizes this succinctly.

إثبات العقل

واحد حقيقي
هيولى

جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the intellect is just another created being among many, with no special status.
Correction: This proof shows the intellect is the first direct emanation from God, distinct from all other beings in its simplicity and independence.

Checkpoint
Why cannot the first emanation be a body, according to the first proof?
A) Because a body is composed, which would necessitate multiplicity in the first rank of emanation
B) Because a body is not independent in existence
C) Because a body requires a soul to act
D) Because a body is an accident

Key Takeaway
The first proof demonstrates that the intellect alone satisfies the conditions of being the first emanation: it is one, simple, and independent in both existence and effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the first creation is the intellect, and you are endowed with intellect, are you using it to recognize God's oneness and your utter dependence on Him, or do you rely on created causes as if they were independent? How will you cultivate deeper intellectual tawhid today?
?
This proof shows that only the intellect is independent in existence and effect. Reflect: in what areas of your life do you act as if you are independent of God? What specific habit will you change to remind yourself that every effect depends directly on Him?
?
The soul depends on the body for its actions, yet you often feel self-sufficient. How does this proof humble your sense of self-reliance? Write one concrete commitment to practice dependence on God alone in a situation where you usually rely on your own strength.

Second Proof: The Producer of a Body Must Be the Intellect
Al-Jurjani eliminates candidates for the producer of a body, concluding it must be the intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof that the producer of a body cannot be God, a body, a soul, a part, or an accident, and must be the intellect.

Core Idea
The producer of a body cannot be any physical or composite entity; only the intellect can.

Al-Jurjani presents a systematic elimination argument. He shows that the agent producing a body like a celestial sphere cannot be any of the familiar candidates—neither the Necessary Being, nor a body, nor a soul, nor a part, nor an accident. Only the intellect remains. This lesson unpacks each step of that elimination.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal English translation carefully. Note the structure: a series of impossibilities leading to a conclusion.
2
Identify the candidates eliminated
The proof eliminates five candidates for the producer of a body: the Necessary (God), a body, a soul, a part of the body, and an accident. List them as you follow the reasoning.
3
Understand each elimination reasoning
For each candidate, understand why it cannot be the producer. The proof uses logical and empirical arguments.
Pay attention to the argument that a body only acts on things spatially related to it (by proximity or facing).
4
Connect to the conclusion
After eliminating all possibilities, the only remaining candidate is the intellect. See how this conclusion follows necessarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني الموجد للجسم كالفلك مثلاً لا يجوز أن يكون هو الواجب لذاته وإلا لأ وجد جزأيه لأن موجد الكل حقيقة يجب أن يكون موجداً لكل واحد من أجزائه فيكون الواجب تعالى مصدر الأثرين في مرتبة واحدة ولا جسماً للآخر إذ الجسم إنما يؤثر فيما له وضع مخصوص بالقياس إليه إما بالمجاورة والقرب أو المحاذاة والمقابلة علم ذلك بالتجربة فإن النار لا تسخن أي جسم آخر كان بل ما يقاربها والشمس لا تضيء إلا ما يقابلها فلو أوجد لوجب أن يفيض صورته على هيولاه، ولو أفاض الصورة على الهيولى لكان للهيولى ذات موجودة وضع قبل الصور وأنه محال لأن وضع الهيولى مستفاد من الصورة التي هي وضع بالذات لكونها في حد نفسها ممتداً في الجهات ولا نفسا لتوقف تأثيرها عليه فإن النفس لا تؤثر إلا بآلات جسمانية فيكون تأثيرها متأخراً عن الجسم فكيف يتصور إيجادها إياه ولا أحد جزايه وإلا لكان ذلك الجزء الموجد للجسم علة للآخر وقد أبطلناه لعدم استقلاله بالوجود دون الآخر فلا يتصور كونه علة للآخر ولا عرضاً لتأخره عنه في الوجود فهو الموجد للجسم العقل
Second: The producer of the body (such as the sphere, for example) cannot be the Necessary in Its essence; otherwise, it would produce its two parts, because the producer of the whole must necessarily be the producer of each one of its parts, and so the Necessary, exalted, would be the source of two effects at one rank. Nor can it be a body for another reason: the body only affects what has a special position relative to it, either by adjacency and proximity, or by facing and opposition. That is known by experience, for fire does not heat any other body except what is near it, and the sun gives light only to what faces it. So if it produced [a body], it would have to emanate its form onto its hyle; and if it emanated the form onto the hyle, then the hyle would have a subsistent essence with a position prior to the form, which is impossible because the position of hyle is derived from the form, which is position by essence since it is extended in dimensions. Nor can it be a soul, because the soul's effect depends on the body, for the soul only acts through bodily organs, so its effect is posterior to the body; how then can it be conceived that it produces it? Nor can it be one of its two parts, for then that part which produced the body would be a cause for the other; and we have already refuted that due to its lack of independence in existence without the other, so it cannot be a cause for the other. Nor can it be an accident, because an accident is posterior to the substance. Hence, the producer of the body is the intellect.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This is the second proof. It argues that the agent that produces a body (like a celestial sphere) cannot be the Necessary of itself (God), because if God directly created a composite body, He would be creating both its parts at once, violating the unity of act. It cannot be a body because bodies only act on what is spatially related to them (near or facing), whereas the first cause is not subject to space. It cannot be a soul because a soul depends on a body for its actions. It cannot be a part of the body because that part would need the other part. It cannot be an accident because accidents are posterior to substance. Therefore, the producer of the body must be the intellect.

Key Terms
الموجد للجسم
فلك
هيولى
صورة
وضع
نفس
عرض
تجربة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof directly proves God's existence.
Correction: This proof assumes God's existence and argues that the first created being (the intellect) is not God, a body, soul, etc., but the intellect.

Checkpoint
Why cannot the producer of a body be a body itself?
A) Because a body cannot produce anything similar to itself
B) Because a body only acts on things that are spatially related to it, but the first cause is not subject to spatial relations
C) Because a body is composed and therefore cannot be a producer
D) Because a body is an accident

Key Takeaway
The producer of a body cannot be any composite or dependent entity; only the intellect, which is simple and immaterial, can be the direct agent of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the producer of the celestial bodies is an immaterial intellect, not any physical cause, in what ways have you been attributing ultimate agency to material things in your daily life? How would your trust shift if you truly believed that the intellect is the only true cause behind every event?
?
The proof eliminates the soul as producer because it depends on the body. Yet you often act as if your soul is independent and self-sufficient. When have you mistaken your own dependence on physical means for self-reliance? What would it mean to acknowledge that your soul itself is created and dependent?
?
You are part of a composite body, just like the sphere. This proof shows that your body's ultimate origin is not from a part of you or from any physical agent. How does that challenge your sense of ownership over your own body? Are you ready to see your body as a gift from an intellect beyond your comprehension, rather than a possession you control?

Objections to the Proofs of the One and Their Answers
Al-Jurjani presents objections to both proofs and replies to them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main objections raised against the two proofs for the oneness of the Necessary Being and how kalam dialectics respond to them.

Core Idea
Kalam objections are dialectical steps, not rejections of the entire doctrine.

In the previous lesson, you encountered two proofs for the oneness of the Necessary Being. Now, al-Jurjani presents objections a proponent might raise and shows how they can be answered. This passage demonstrates the dialectical method of kalam, where every claim is tested against alternatives, and the aim is to refine the proof rather than abandon it. Pay attention to how the objector proposes alternative first emanations (body, soul, attribute) and challenges the premises of the second proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow. Then read the English translation. Notice that it begins with 'Objection' and presents several 'why may it not be' alternatives.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the two proofs being objected
The objector references 'the first proof' and 'the second proof'. Recall from earlier lessons what these proofs are: first proof from the principle 'only one proceeds from the One', second proof from the nature of bodies affecting only what is spatially related.
3
List the alternatives proposed
For the first proof, the objector suggests the first emanation could be a body (with parts), a soul, or an attribute of God. For the second proof, the objector suggests the producer could be a body or a soul, and also reuses the first proof's objection about the two parts.
Note how each alternative is presented with its own reasoning.
4
Examine the responses
Al-Jurjani responds to each objection: for the attribute alternative, he says it will be refuted later; for the second proof, he denies the premise, criticizes induction, and grants for the sake of argument but still objects.
The responses are brief and sometimes incomplete, signaling that the full refutation will come later.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتراض بناء على تسليم أن الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا الواحد أما على الوجه الأول فلم لا يجوز أن يكون أول صادر هو الجسم بأن يصدر أحد جزأيه عن الواجب تعالى ابتداء وبواسطته يصدر الآخر وقد صرحوا بأن الصورة جزء لعلة الهيولى وليس يلزم من كونها غنية في مدخلية التأثير عن الهيولى كونها غنية في وجودها متشخصة عنها وإن سلم ذلك فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الصادر الأول نفساً ولا يلزم من توقف تصرفها في البدن على تعلقها به توقف إيجاده مطلقاً على ذلك التعلق فيجوز أن يوجد الجسم بلا تعلق هو منشأ للتصرف والتدبير وإن سلم فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الصادر الأول صفة قائمة بذات الله تعالى ودليلهم على عدم زيادة الصفات سنبطله وأما على الوجه الثاني فلم لا يجوز أن يكون الموجد للجسم جسماً قوله إنما يؤثر الجسم فيما له وضع بالنسبة إليه ممنوع والاستقراء على سبيل التجربة كما ذكرتم لا يفيد العموم لأنه استقراء ناقص سلمناه لكن قد يكون الموجد نفساً توجده أولاً ثم تتعلق به سلمناه لكن قد يكون هو الواجب بأن يوجد أحد جزأيه ابتداء وبتوسطه الجزء الآخر لما مر في الاعتراض على الوجه الأول
Objection: Based on the acceptance that only one proceeds from the One: As for the first proof, why may it not be that the first proceeding is the body, by one of its two parts proceeding from the Exalted God initially, and through it the other part proceeds? They have stated that the form is part of the cause of the hyle, and it does not follow from its being independent in the mode of effect [without hyle] that it is independent in its existence individually separated from it. And if that is granted, then why may it not be that the first proceeding is a soul? It does not follow from the dependence of its action in the body on its attachment to it that its production [of the body] is absolutely dependent on that attachment; so it is possible that the body exists without an attachment that is the origin of action and management. And if that is granted, then why may it not be that the first proceeding is an attribute subsisting in the essence of God? And we will refute their evidence for the lack of multiplicity of attributes. As for the second proof, why may it not be that the producer of the body is a body? Their statement 'the body only affects what has a position relative to it' is denied, and the induction by way of experience as you mentioned does not yield universality because it is an incomplete induction. We grant it, but it may be that the producer is a soul that produces it first and then attaches to it. We grant it, but it may be that it is the Necessary, by producing one of its two parts initially and through it the other part, as passed in the objection to the first proof.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage presents objections to the two proofs and their answers. The objector challenges the first proof by suggesting that the first thing could be a body if one of its parts emanates first and then the other through it. They also suggest it could be a soul or an attribute of God. For the second proof, they argue that a body could be the producer, denying the claim that bodies only affect spatially related things, or that a soul could produce the body. The author responds briefly, indicating that some of these will be refuted later. The passage shows the dialectical nature of kalam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Objections in kalam are meant to reject the entire position.
Correction: Objections are used to test and strengthen arguments; even when granted, they do not invalidate the proof but lead to further refinement.

Checkpoint
In the objection to the first proof, what alternative is suggested for the first emanation?
A) That it could be a body with one part emanating first and the other through it
B) That it could be an accident
C) That it could be a purely physical force
D) That it could be the soul of the cosmos

Key Takeaway
The dialectical method of kalam uses objections to refine proofs, not to reject them outright.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter objections to your belief in tawheed, do you immediately dismiss them or do you engage with them as the kalam scholars did? This lesson shows that objections can strengthen faith. What objection to your own faith have you been avoiding, and will you commit to studying it this week?
?
The objector in this passage accepts the principle 'only one proceeds from the One' but still raises possibilities. Are there any aspects of God's oneness that you find difficult to reconcile with the diversity of creation? How can the dialectical method help you deepen your understanding rather than avoid the difficulty?
?
If you were to defend the oneness of God to a skeptic, would you anticipate objections? This lesson shows that anticipating objections is part of a robust proof. Are you willing to invest time in learning the intellectual tools of kalam to strengthen your own certainty? What is one step you will take this week to equip yourself?

Causality and Created Things

Emanation of Intellects, Souls, and Spheres
Al-Jurjani describes the threefold emanation from the first intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Neoplatonic emanation scheme as presented by al-Jurjani, particularly the threefold emanation from the first intellect based on its three aspects.

Core Idea
From the first intellect's three aspects emanate intellect, soul, and body.

This lesson explores the intricate metaphysical framework of emanation that the philosophers (falasifa) adopted. Al-Jurjani explains how from the First Intellect, by virtue of its three aspects—existence in itself, necessity by another, and possibility—three distinct realities proceed: an intellect, a soul, and the first sphere. This lays the foundation for the entire hierarchy of celestial beings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the logical flow from the first intellect to its emanations.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the three considerations
Find where al-Jurjani lists the three considerations of the first intellect: its existence, its necessity by another, and its possibility. Understand each term.
These correspond to different metaphysical aspects.
3
Match each consideration to its emanation
See how each consideration gives rise to a specific entity: existence → intellect, necessity → soul, possibility → body (first sphere). Note the hierarchy: intellect is noblest, then soul, then body.
This ordering reflects the principle of attribution of the noblest to the noblest.
4
Recognize the recurrent pattern
Notice that the same triad emanates from each subsequent intellect: from the second intellect proceed a third intellect, a second soul, and a second sphere. This establishes a chain.
This explains the multiplicity of celestial spheres and souls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثاني : في ترتيب الموجودات في ترتيب الموجودات على رأيهم قالوا إذا ثبت أن الصادر الأول عقل فله اعتبارات ثلاثة وجوده في نفسه ووجوبه بالغير وإمكانه لذاته فيصدر عنه بكل اعتبار أمر فباعتبار وجوده يصدر عقل وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير يصدر نفس وباعتبار إمكانه يصدر جسم هو الفلك الأول وإنما قلنا إن صدورها عنه على هذا الوجه إسناد للأشراف إلى الجهة الأشرف والأخس إلى الأخس فإنه أحرى وأخلق وكذلك يصدر من العقل الثاني عقل ثالث ونفس ثانية وفلك ثان
The Second Intention: On the Ordering of Existent Things. On the ordering of existent things according to their view. They said: If it is established that the first proceeding is an intellect, then it has three considerations: its existence in itself, its necessity by another, and its possibility in itself. So from each consideration an entity proceeds: by virtue of its existence, an intellect proceeds; by virtue of its necessity by another, a soul proceeds; and by virtue of its possibility, a body proceeds, which is the first sphere. And we say that their proceeding from it in this manner is attribution of the noblest to the noblest side and the basest to the basest, for that is more fitting and more proper. Similarly, from the second intellect proceeds a third intellect, a second soul, and a second sphere.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage describes the Neoplatonic emanation scheme adopted by the philosophers. Once the first intellect is established, it has three aspects: its own existence, its being necessary through another (God), and its intrinsic possibility. From each aspect emanates a specific type of being: intellect, soul, and body (the first sphere). This principle is applied recursively: from each subsequent intellect, another triad emanates, producing a hierarchy of intellects, souls, and celestial spheres.

Key Terms
ترتيب الموجودات
اعتبارات ثلاثة
وجود
وجوب بالغير
إمكان
فلك
نفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This emanation scheme is often taken as a literal creation story, where God directly creates each being.
Correction: It is actually a metaphysical framework explaining the dependence of all things on the First Principle through necessary emanation, not voluntary creation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what proceeds from the first intellect by virtue of its possibility in itself?
A) Another intellect
B) A soul
C) A body which is the first sphere
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The first intellect, by its three aspects, gives rise to the triad of intellect, soul, and sphere, establishing a hierarchical emanation that repeats at each level.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your own existence, like the first intellect, is only possible in itself and necessary through God, what would change in how you view your daily successes and failures? Would you still take pride in your achievements as if they were your own?
?
The passage attributes nobility to the intellectual aspect and baseness to the bodily sphere. Look at your own life: which parts do you consider 'noble' and which 'base'? Are you living as if the 'base' parts are outside of God's control or as if they too proceed from Him?
?
The philosophers say that from the first intellect's very nature, things emanate. What if your actions, thoughts, and intentions also emanate from your inner state? Are the 'emanations' of your life—your words and deeds—noble or base? What does that say about the state of your heart before God?

The Three Considerations and Emanation Chain
Explanation of the emanation scheme from the first intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three considerations of the first intellect and how the philosophers derive the emanation of intellects, souls, and bodies from them, down to the Active Intellect.

Core Idea
Three considerations of the first intellect generate the entire cosmos.

The philosophers argue that from the first intellect, which is the first creation, three aspects yield three distinct effects: another intellect, a soul, and the first sphere. This lesson presents that scheme and its extension down to the Active Intellect that governs our world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the three considerations and their outcomes.
Notice the technical term 'اعتبارات' (considerations).
2
Identify the three emanations
Match each consideration (existence, necessity by another, possibility) to its issued effect (intellect, soul, body).
3
Trace the chain
Understand how the same pattern repeats from the first to the tenth intellect, each producing a lower intellect, soul, and sphere.
The tenth intellect is the Active Intellect, which governs the sublunar world.
4
Examine the Active Intellect's role
Note how the Active Intellect acts on the matter of the sublunar world through celestial motions and preparations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ المقصد الثاني : في ترتيب الموجودات ]
( في ترتيب الموجودات على رأيهم. قالوا : إذا ثبت أن الصادر الأول عقل فله اعتبارات ثلاثة : وجوده في نفسه، ووجوبه بالغير، وإمكانه لذاته، فيصدر عنه بكل اعتبار أمر. فباعتبار وجوده ) يصدر ( عقل وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير يصدر (نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه ) يصدر ( جسم ) هو الفلك الأول . وإنما قلنا إن صدورها عنه على هذا الوجه إسناد للأشراف إلى الجهة الأشرف والأخس إلى الأخس فإنه أحرى وأخلق، وكذلك ) يصدر (من) العقل ( الثاني عقل) ثالث ( ونفس) ثانية (وفلك ) ثان وهكذا ) إلى ( العقل ( العاشر ) الذي هو في مرتبة التاسع من الأفلاك أعني فلك القمر ( ويسمى العقل الفعال) المؤثر في هيولى العالم السفلي ( المفيض للصور ) والنفوس والأعراض على العناصر) البسيطة ( و ) على ( المركبات ( منها ( بسبب ما يحصل الاستعدادات المسببة عن الحركات (الفلكية والاتصالات الكوكبية وأوضاعها الاعتراض ) أن يقال : ( هذه الاعتبارات إن كانت وجودية فلا بد لها من مصادر متعددة ( وإلا بطل قولكم : الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا الواحد فيبطل حينئذ ) ( أصل دليلكم وإن كانت اعتبارية امتنع أن تصير جزءاً مصدراً للأمور الوجودية ) وقد يجاب عنه بأنها ليست جزءا من المؤثر بل هي شرط للتأثير والشرط قد يكون أمراً اعتبارياً لكن مثل هذه الاعتبارات من السلوب والإضافات عارضة للمبدأ الأول فيجوز أن تكون بحسبها مصدراً لأمور متعددة كالمعلول الأول، وذلك مناف المذهبهم الذي بنوا عليه كلامهم في ترتيب الموجودات ) وحديث إسناد الأشراف إلى الأشراف خطابي ( لا يتلفت إليه في المطالب العلمية ( وإسناد الفلك الثامن مع ما فيه من الكواكب المختلفة ( المقادير المتكثرة كثرة لا تحصى ( إلى جهة واحدة ) في العقل الثاني كما زعموه ( مشكل) جداً . ( وكذلك إسناد الصور والأعراض التي في مع كثرتها ) الفائتة عن الحصر ) إلى العقل الفعال) مشكل أيضاً ( وبالجملة فلا يخفى على الفطن المنصف ضعف ما اعتمدوا عليه في هذا المطلب التالي ) وفي الملخص إنهم خبطوا فتارة اعتبروا في العقل الأول جهتين: وجوده، وجعلوه علة العقل وإمكانه وجعلوه علة ،الفلك ومنهم من اعتبر بدلهما تعقله لوجوده وإمكانه علة لعقل وفلك، وتارة اعتبروا فيه كثرة من ثلاثة أوجه كما ذكر في متن الكتاب وتارة من أربعة أوجه فزادوا علمه بذلك الغير وجعلوا إمكانه علة لهيولى الفلك وعلمه علة لصورته فظهر أن العقول عاجزة عن إدراك نظام الموجودات على ما هي عليه في نفس الأمر.
[The second objective: On the arrangement of existents] (On the arrangement of existents according to their view. They said: When it is established that the first issued is an intellect, it has three considerations: its existence in itself, its necessity by another, and its possibility in itself. So from each consideration an affair issues from it. By consideration of its existence) issues (an intellect, by consideration of its necessity by another issues a soul, and by consideration of its possibility issues a body, which is the first sphere. And we only say that their issuance from it in this manner is an attribution of the nobler to the noblest aspect and the baser to the basest, for that is more fitting and appropriate. Similarly) from the second intellect issues a third intellect, a second soul, and a second sphere, and so on) up to the tenth intellect, which is in the rank of the ninth sphere, I mean the sphere of the moon, and is called the Active Intellect, which acts on the matter of the sublunar world, emanating the forms, souls, and accidents upon the simple elements and upon the compounds from them, due to the preparations caused by celestial motions, planetary conjunctions, and their positions. Objection: It may be said: These considerations, if they are existent, then they must have multiple sources; otherwise your statement 'the One does not issue from Him except one' is nullified, and then your proof foundation is nullified. And if they are non-existent, it is impossible that they become part of a source for existent things. And it may be answered that they are not part of the effecting factor but are a condition for the effect, and the condition may be a non-existent thing. But such considerations, being negations and relations, are accidents of the first principle, so it may be through them that it is a source for multiple things like the first effect. That contradicts their school, upon which they based their discourse on the arrangement of existents. And the talk about attributing the nobler to the nobler is rhetorical, not to be regarded in scientific inquiries. And attributing the eighth sphere with its various planets of many different sizes beyond count to a single aspect in the second intellect as they claim is very problematic. Similarly, attributing the forms and accidents which are in their multiplicity beyond enumeration to the Active Intellect is also problematic. In short, it is not hidden from the intelligent and impartial person the weakness of what they relied upon in this following inquiry. And in al-Mulakhkhas, they confused: sometimes they considered in the first intellect two aspects: its existence, making it the cause of the intellect, and its possibility, making it the cause of the sphere. Some instead considered its intellection of its existence and possibility as the cause of the intellect and sphere. Sometimes they considered multiplicity in it from three aspects as mentioned in the text of the book, and sometimes from four aspects, adding its knowledge of that other, making its possibility the cause of the sphere's matter and its knowledge the cause of its form. So it became clear that the intellects are incapable of apprehending the system of existents as they are in themselves.)
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the emanationist cosmology attributed to the philosophers (al-ḥukamā'), and then a critique. It begins with the heading 'The second objective: on the arrangement of existents.' The author states the philosophers' view: given that the first issued from God is an intellect, that intellect has three considerations: its existence in itself (which is necessary by another), its necessity by the other (God), and its possibility in itself. From each consideration, something issues: from its existence issues a second intellect, from its necessity by the other issues a soul, and from its possibility issues a body (the first sphere). The author notes that this attributes the nobler effect to the nobler aspect. Then it describes the chain down to the tenth intellect (the Active Intellect) which governs the sublunar world. A crucial objection follows: if the considerations are real (wujūdiyya), they would require multiple sources, contradicting the principle 'from the One only one proceeds'; but if they are merely mental (iʿtibāriyya), they cannot be sources of real things. The answer given is that they are not parts of the cause but conditions, and conditions may be mental; but this contradicts the philosophers' own school. The author then dismisses the rhetorical appeal to nobility and points out difficulties: the eighth sphere's myriad stars cannot be traced to a single aspect; the Active Intellect cannot account for all forms and accidents. The passage ends with a summary of inconsistencies in the philosophers' various schemes, concluding that the intellects are incapable of grasping the true order of existents. The teacher should note that the author is presenting and refuting a philosophical theory, not endorsing it.

العقل الفعال
هيولى العالم السفلي
استعدادات
حركات فلكية

According to the philosophers' emanation scheme, what issues from the first intellect by consideration of its possibility?
A) A second intellect
B) A soul
C) A body (the first sphere)
D) The Active Intellect

Key Takeaway
The philosophers derive the multiplicity of the cosmos from three aspects of the first intellect, but this scheme faces objections and criticisms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate the vastness of creation, do you tend to see it as a mechanical chain of causes or as the direct, personal act of a loving Creator? How does your view affect your reliance on Him in daily trials?
?
If emanation were true, God would create by necessity, not by will. Have you ever acted as if God's care for you is automatic, like a law of nature, rather than a deliberate act of mercy? What would change if you truly believed every blessing is a free gift?
?
The philosophers' scheme reduces the intellect to a mere step in a process. Do you treat your own intellect as a tool for submitting to God's revelation, or as an independent judge over it? Ask yourself honestly: in which areas of your life do you trust your reasoning more than scripture?

Objections to the Emanation Scheme
Presentation of the objection and critique of the emanation scheme.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objection that if the considerations are existent they violate the principle of oneness, and the response that they are conditions, along with the author's critique showing the scheme's inconsistencies.

Core Idea
The philosophers' own principle undermines their emanation scheme.

After presenting the emanation scheme, the author raises a powerful objection: if the three considerations are real, they require multiple sources, contradicting the principle that from the One only one proceeds. If they are merely mental, they cannot cause real effects. The philosophers' attempted answer fails. This lesson unpacks the objection, the response, and the author's critique highlighting further problems.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Understand the dilemma: if considerations are existent, they need multiple sources; if non-existent, they cannot cause effects.
2
Analyze the answer
The philosophers claim the considerations are conditions, not parts of the cause, and conditions can be mental.
But the author notes this contradicts their own school.
3
Examine the author's critiques
The author points out three problems: the rhetorical nature of the 'nobler' attribution, the difficulty of the eighth sphere, and the Active Intellect's inability to account for all forms.
4
Review the summary of inconsistencies
The author concludes by noting the philosophers' various confused schemes, showing their inability to grasp the true system.

[ المقصد الثاني : في ترتيب الموجودات ]
( في ترتيب الموجودات على رأيهم. قالوا : إذا ثبت أن الصادر الأول عقل فله اعتبارات ثلاثة : وجوده في نفسه، ووجوبه بالغير، وإمكانه لذاته، فيصدر عنه بكل اعتبار أمر. فباعتبار وجوده ) يصدر ( عقل وباعتبار وجوبه بالغير يصدر (نفس، وباعتبار إمكانه ) يصدر ( جسم ) هو الفلك الأول . وإنما قلنا إن صدورها عنه على هذا الوجه إسناد للأشراف إلى الجهة الأشرف والأخس إلى الأخس فإنه أحرى وأخلق، وكذلك ) يصدر (من) العقل ( الثاني عقل) ثالث ( ونفس) ثانية (وفلك ) ثان وهكذا ) إلى ( العقل ( العاشر ) الذي هو في مرتبة التاسع من الأفلاك أعني فلك القمر ( ويسمى العقل الفعال) المؤثر في هيولى العالم السفلي ( المفيض للصور ) والنفوس والأعراض على العناصر) البسيطة ( و ) على ( المركبات ( منها ( بسبب ما يحصل الاستعدادات المسببة عن الحركات (الفلكية والاتصالات الكوكبية وأوضاعها الاعتراض ) أن يقال : ( هذه الاعتبارات إن كانت وجودية فلا بد لها من مصادر متعددة ( وإلا بطل قولكم : الواحد لا يصدر عنه إلا الواحد فيبطل حينئذ ) ( أصل دليلكم وإن كانت اعتبارية امتنع أن تصير جزءاً مصدراً للأمور الوجودية ) وقد يجاب عنه بأنها ليست جزءا من المؤثر بل هي شرط للتأثير والشرط قد يكون أمراً اعتبارياً لكن مثل هذه الاعتبارات من السلوب والإضافات عارضة للمبدأ الأول فيجوز أن تكون بحسبها مصدراً لأمور متعددة كالمعلول الأول، وذلك مناف المذهبهم الذي بنوا عليه كلامهم في ترتيب الموجودات ) وحديث إسناد الأشراف إلى الأشراف خطابي ( لا يتلفت إليه في المطالب العلمية ( وإسناد الفلك الثامن مع ما فيه من الكواكب المختلفة ( المقادير المتكثرة كثرة لا تحصى ( إلى جهة واحدة ) في العقل الثاني كما زعموه ( مشكل) جداً . ( وكذلك إسناد الصور والأعراض التي في مع كثرتها ) الفائتة عن الحصر ) إلى العقل الفعال) مشكل أيضاً ( وبالجملة فلا يخفى على الفطن المنصف ضعف ما اعتمدوا عليه في هذا المطلب التالي ) وفي الملخص إنهم خبطوا فتارة اعتبروا في العقل الأول جهتين: وجوده، وجعلوه علة العقل وإمكانه وجعلوه علة ،الفلك ومنهم من اعتبر بدلهما تعقله لوجوده وإمكانه علة لعقل وفلك، وتارة اعتبروا فيه كثرة من ثلاثة أوجه كما ذكر في متن الكتاب وتارة من أربعة أوجه فزادوا علمه بذلك الغير وجعلوا إمكانه علة لهيولى الفلك وعلمه علة لصورته فظهر أن العقول عاجزة عن إدراك نظام الموجودات على ما هي عليه في نفس الأمر.
[The second objective: On the arrangement of existents] (On the arrangement of existents according to their view. They said: When it is established that the first issued is an intellect, it has three considerations: its existence in itself, its necessity by another, and its possibility in itself. So from each consideration an affair issues from it. By consideration of its existence) issues (an intellect, by consideration of its necessity by another issues a soul, and by consideration of its possibility issues a body, which is the first sphere. And we only say that their issuance from it in this manner is an attribution of the nobler to the noblest aspect and the baser to the basest, for that is more fitting and appropriate. Similarly) from the second intellect issues a third intellect, a second soul, and a second sphere, and so on) up to the tenth intellect, which is in the rank of the ninth sphere, I mean the sphere of the moon, and is called the Active Intellect, which acts on the matter of the sublunar world, emanating the forms, souls, and accidents upon the simple elements and upon the compounds from them, due to the preparations caused by celestial motions, planetary conjunctions, and their positions. Objection: It may be said: These considerations, if they are existent, then they must have multiple sources; otherwise your statement 'the One does not issue from Him except one' is nullified, and then your proof foundation is nullified. And if they are non-existent, it is impossible that they become part of a source for existent things. And it may be answered that they are not part of the effecting factor but are a condition for the effect, and the condition may be a non-existent thing. But such considerations, being negations and relations, are accidents of the first principle, so it may be through them that it is a source for multiple things like the first effect. That contradicts their school, upon which they based their discourse on the arrangement of existents. And the talk about attributing the nobler to the nobler is rhetorical, not to be regarded in scientific inquiries. And attributing the eighth sphere with its various planets of many different sizes beyond count to a single aspect in the second intellect as they claim is very problematic. Similarly, attributing the forms and accidents which are in their multiplicity beyond enumeration to the Active Intellect is also problematic. In short, it is not hidden from the intelligent and impartial person the weakness of what they relied upon in this following inquiry. And in al-Mulakhkhas, they confused: sometimes they considered in the first intellect two aspects: its existence, making it the cause of the intellect, and its possibility, making it the cause of the sphere. Some instead considered its intellection of its existence and possibility as the cause of the intellect and sphere. Sometimes they considered multiplicity in it from three aspects as mentioned in the text of the book, and sometimes from four aspects, adding its knowledge of that other, making its possibility the cause of the sphere's matter and its knowledge the cause of its form. So it became clear that the intellects are incapable of apprehending the system of existents as they are in themselves.)
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the emanationist cosmology attributed to the philosophers (al-ḥukamā'), and then a critique. It begins with the heading 'The second objective: on the arrangement of existents.' The author states the philosophers' view: given that the first issued from God is an intellect, that intellect has three considerations: its existence in itself (which is necessary by another), its necessity by the other (God), and its possibility in itself. From each consideration, something issues: from its existence issues a second intellect, from its necessity by the other issues a soul, and from its possibility issues a body (the first sphere). The author notes that this attributes the nobler effect to the nobler aspect. Then it describes the chain down to the tenth intellect (the Active Intellect) which governs the sublunar world. A crucial objection follows: if the considerations are real (wujūdiyya), they would require multiple sources, contradicting the principle 'from the One only one proceeds'; but if they are merely mental (iʿtibāriyya), they cannot be sources of real things. The answer given is that they are not parts of the cause but conditions, and conditions may be mental; but this contradicts the philosophers' own school. The author then dismisses the rhetorical appeal to nobility and points out difficulties: the eighth sphere's myriad stars cannot be traced to a single aspect; the Active Intellect cannot account for all forms and accidents. The passage ends with a summary of inconsistencies in the philosophers' various schemes, concluding that the intellects are incapable of grasping the true order of existents. The teacher should note that the author is presenting and refuting a philosophical theory, not endorsing it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The philosophers' answer that considerations are conditions is logically sound.
Correction: The author shows that such conditions are accidents of the first principle, which contradicts the philosophers' own metaphysical commitments.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the objection against the emanation scheme?
A) The Active Intellect does not exist
B) The considerations either require multiple sources or cannot cause effects
C) The first intellect is not a unity
D) The spheres are too many

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' emanation scheme is internally inconsistent and fails to explain the multiplicity of the cosmos.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you try to understand Allah's creation, do you trust your own reasoning more than revelation? In what specific area of your life does this lesson call you to submit your intellect to divine wisdom?
?
The author shows that even the brightest philosophers failed to grasp the true system of existence. How does this humble your own assumptions about what you 'know'? What one assumption about how God works are you holding onto that might need to be surrendered?
?
You may not be a philosopher, but do you ever find yourself insisting that things 'must' work a certain way based on your own logic? What would it look like to let go of that insistence and say, 'I don't know, but Allah knows best'?
